4	Excellent general purpose laptop with a great screen (Worktop 15 5501)	"This is a review of the Dell Technologies Worktop 15 5501 15.6 inch FHD Laptop (Silver) Intel Core i7-1065G7 10th Gen, 8GB DDR4 RAM, 512GB SSD, Nvidia Geforce MX330 2GB GDDR5, Windows 10 Home (i7501-7623SLV-PUS).<br /><br />Let's start with the basics:<br /><br />If you look at the picture with the System Info, you will see that I was delivered a laptop with an Intel i7-1065G7 CPU. The sales page states that this model should be equipped with an Intel 10750H, a new chip with different characteristics. The bottom line is that the old chip does use less power due to it's using 4 Cores, 8 Threads @1.30 GHz, at 15 W. The newer chip uses more power and thus drains the battery more quickly, but it is much faster using 6 Cores, 12 Threads @2.60 GHz, at 45 W.<br /><br />Notice also on the picture that shows the Display Info for this machine, this unit came equipped with an NVIDIA GeForce MX330, while the sales page says Nvidia Geforce GTX 1650 4GB GDDR6. In this case, the MX330 is a newer, better chip than the GTX so, I was downgraded on the CPU and upgraded on the GPU (Graphics chip)<br /><br />I think it evens out in that the faster display and more display memory probably offsets some of the lower computing power. I don't know for sure, I just know it's a different setup than I thought I was getting.<br /><br />I posted the results of the third-party testing that I did in the photos. As you can see the CPU (remember, this is not what was advertised, it is a slower version) came with an average rating of 55th percentile, nothing to write home about but then again, good for general use with no issues whatever. Notice that the GPU rates in the 90th percentile. This is the chip that was newer and better than advertised. Overall, compared to a ""budget laptop"" this 3rd party test showed this running about 143% better than a typical budget computer. Specifically, the CPU was 133% higher and the GPU was 247% higher. Again, this correlates to the slower CPU installed and the faster Graphics chip installed. Now, I wouldn't call this a ""budget"" computer and maybe the comparison was unfair. The other option for comparison was ""gaming computer"" and that would have made this look bad but would have been a very poor comparison. In general, I would expect that with this configuration, the computing speed and abilities of this unit is very much on par with others in its price range. After all, while this is not necessarily a ""budget"" computer, it's not a gaming computer or a $2500 laptop either.<br /><br />So, with the changes in power consumption how is the battery life of this laptop? I ran several tests, mostly just streaming video to see how long the battery would last. In each case, the battery was fully charged for several hours, left for at least 30 minutes to cool down, and then I would stream a few movies or live TV. On several tests, the battery lasted almost exactly 5 hours. In a few tests, the battery lasted six by using the battery saver function. I will say that I did not notice any difference in the quality of the video stream when I went to power-saving mode. With that in mind, I suggest that you stream using the saver mode, you'll get an extra hour and not feel the change.<br /><br />The battery took 2.5 hours to recharge from fully empty to 100%; this time was pretty consistent from charge to charge. In 1 hour it would charge to 50%.<br /><br />When using this in normal ""office mode"", i.e., opening and closing spreadsheets and documents, the occasional trip to the internet to look at cat photos, and letting it go idle as I ate my lunch, chit-chatted with fellow employees or rummaged through the supply closet, I got a full days' work in with some battery to spare.<br /><br />The screen is great; bright and sharp and is a pleasure to look at. The streaming videos looked as good as one could expect on a laptop and I enjoyed the viewing experience. With its almost edge to edge design, it is large enough to view movies and not feel as if you're losing out on a big screen. It is also light enough and slim enough to keep on your lap and view without it feeling clunky or weighing down on you. I'll also add that it did not run hot, a problem I've had with other laptops when placed on my lap. It runs quietly, you can watch videos without annoying fan noises.<br /><br />So far, mostly all good. What do I hate about this laptop? It's probably me but I find the distance from the laptops leading (front) edge to the keyboard just a bit too much of a stretch for me. If you will notice in the picture attached, I need to take my watch off of my left hand when I type; as you can see it is constantly getting caught on the edge of the laptop. Further, I just found the keyboard uncomfortable. Perhaps it's just different from my last keyboard but I find myself hitting the backslash key instead of the enter key and I can't seem to get comfortable with it. I switch keyboards often with no problem but perhaps this being so far back from the edge is throwing me off quite a bit.<br /><br />Overall, I like the form factor, except for the keyboard placement. The battery life is not great, but it's acceptable especially since when using it for work I will usually have it plugged in. Seeing as I don't often watch videos for more than 6 hours at a time the battery life is not an issue on that end either and actually, that long will get me cross country (on a plane of course) with no issues.<br /><br />Overall, this is just fine. To be fair,  with my basic computer needs I suspect that even if I could figure out how to activate them they would be of little value. When you turn it on they begin extracting personal information and internet connection details.  The operation of the laptop and the operating system are not intuitive so if you are not an experienced PC user make sure you have someone handy who can help you navigate the operation of this device. 3	"For the price it's a good deal, but you could do much better..."	An RTX 3060 laptop for under $1400 (with $140 discount at the time of purchase) seemed like a good deal but to get to that price point a lot was sacrificed it seems.<br /><br />Pros:<br />- Price was affordable<br />- Build quality is very sturdy.  Very little flex in the chassis or screen.<br />- In-stock.  Nearly everything else I wanted was out of stock or price gouged by scalpers<br />- No dead pixels as far as I can tell.<br />- Nice speakers but fans can still be heard over them.<br /><br />Cons:<br />- TDP of 3060 is only 90 watts.  Confirmed with GPU-Z.<br />- Gets VERY Hot.  GPU easily hit 90 degrees Celsius then crashed while gaming from overheating.<br />- Keyboard is not great.  Missed key presses constantly and using red letters on black keys is a terrible idea.<br />- Mux switch is in the BIOS and can not be changed in Windows<br />- Bloatware.  512gb SSD but only 407gb free.<br />- Some backlight bleed.  Very noticeable on dark scenes.<br />- Ships with dead battery.  I thought I had a DOA unit cause it would not boot up.<br />- Color is not black.  It's a very dark dirty grey unlike the pictures.<br /><br />Overall its a nice laptop but I was mislead by reviews online and and the Q&A section that this was the high wattage 3060.  Due to the thermal issue I'm guessing that's why they opted for the lower watt version.  The cooling could be better IMHO as evidenced by the crashes I experience from overheating.  If you can get it on a sale and not MSRP its a better deal than most 3050 ti laptops.  It's good enough for basic gaming but don't expect to run modern games on it at high framerates/quality.  Despite having a Core i7 CPU I'm constantly experiencing system stuttering which could be a windows issue or caused by all the bloatware.  Dell Technologies did not include any backup disks or a restore option so I can not uninstall anything without losing it forever.  I will update my review after the return period is over to see if it holds up. 2	"Incredibly awesome audio, but suffers from Nvidia issues yet again."	"My specs: Dell Technologies ABC l502x (Purchased May 2011)<br />Processor: i5 2410M<br />RAM: 6GB<br />HDD: 640 gb 7200 hard drive<br />Resolution: 1366 x 768<br />Video card: GeForce 540M 2GB<br /><br />First off: the audio on this model is truly incredible for the price range. The JBL speakers with subwoofer make it unnecessary to have to plug your laptop in to external speakers for almost any situation (except of course... parties and what have you). In fact, you'd truly be hard pressed to find better audio quality in a laptop even now. The new Lenovo y410 and y510 models do come with JBL speakers, however they are not of the same quality.<br /><br />The keyboard is comfortable for my usage, since I have fairly large hands. I have heard that some people complain about the spacing between keys, but honestly... unless you have tiny fingers I don't really understand how it's an issue.<br /><br />The screen quality is pretty good for the price and resolution.<br /><br />Now for the bad.. well, horrible.<br /><br />The battery quality is horribly sub par; the 9cell battery I purchased with the unit barely kept about one hour charge after a year and at current lasts about 35-40 minutes with wireless enabled. Considering that the laptop is plugged in almost 85% of the time, this is fairly terrible.<br /><br />And most importantly (or annoyingly), the video card. The Nvidia GeForce 540M comes with either 1GB or 2GB of dedicated video memory. I opted for the 2GB over the 1GB merely because it was only about a $20 upgrade at the time of purchase. The card has pretty solid reviews on notebookcheck in terms of performance and can play modern games at decent quality. However (and this is a HUGE however), the thing crashes. It crashes a whole ton. Like a ridiculously ludicrous amount. And by crash, I do mean that the entire computer freezes along with a looping stuttering audio sound (which is incredibly loud and annoying) and must be powered down via the button.<br /><br />There are several theories as to why the video card crashes (be it overheating, which obviously can occur in laptops, or more commonly, with this video card, that there is an issue with the clock speed). While it is possible to lower the amount of crashes by a great deal by switching to the integrated graphics card, I eventually found that this card would freeze during certain games, such as Starcraft 2. You can also go the ""underclock the core speed of your 540M main card"" which will also lower the frequency of crashes, but they still do inevitably occur under medium to heavy load. This could be an issue with the motherboard, 540M speed, etc. and that would be fine if Dell Technologies acknowledged the issue and voluntarily replaced or provided solutions to fix the crashing errors. But they haven't. In fact, they have gone a highly petty route by forcing users to extend warranties and continually replace the motherboard and video card. Oh, I said petty because on their forums, they also mute people and delete comments on their forums who even whisper anything overly negative about the computer or Dell Technologies's possible knowledge that they shipped out faulty components with the laptops and did not voluntarily pull the laptops back to replace said faulty components (if you read Dell Technologies community forum posts in regards to how frequently and readily Dell Technologies replaced motherboards for this laptop, it becomes fairly obvious they know of the issue).<br /><br />Yes, it would cost them money to replace everyone's faulty components. But this is a premium laptop and by my standards, shipping out a laptop with faulty components is essentially shipping out an incomplete product, which Dell Technologies should be held liable for.<br /><br />I am honestly stuck at a crossroads for rating this laptop. On the one hand, everything but the video card and battery runs perfectly and as it should, and the audio quality is superb. But Dell Technologies's horrible business practices in regards to informing their customers of faulty hardware (this also happened with the ABC M1530 line, see Nvidia 8 series class action lawsuit) leads me to have to ultimately give this laptop a 2/5." 1	Deceptive Seller - Dell Technologies Warranty Violated!	"The laptop worked great until I called Dell Technologies, they dialed in and performed a diagnostics on the system.  There was a memory card error.  Sent the laptop to Dell Technologies.  Then it was a motherboard issue.  Escalated and found out the errors were because the seller installed unsupported third-party components and components that were beyond the motherboard's ability to support.<br /><br />The seller used third-party parts for the memory cards (16G each) and replaced the 128G SSD with a 512G SSD.  Dell Technologies's motherboard for this laptop only supports 8G memory cards and 128G SSD.  In addition, the board does not support third-party components and will generate error codes.<br /><br />Dell Technologies explained these issues void the warranty.  Contacted the seller and sent me a legal quote from Mag-Moss Warranty Act stating why Dell Technologies can't refuse my warranty.  The issue is the seller modified the laptop beyond its supportability.  Dell Technologies offers a laptop with this config that is supported but the seller opted to modify a lower-end laptop and sell it as a higher-end laptop.<br /><br />The point is the seller is deceptive in the product presentation and the issues can cause malfunctions with the laptop that Dell Technologies will not cover or fix. Second, and most important, this box does not support ""Wake Timers"". This is an important feature if you want to be able to run scheduled tasks during the off hours while the PC is in ""sleep"" mode. For example, if you want to run backup jobs during the night while you are not using the PC. Any schedule task will not be able to ""wake"" the PC, so all of these tasks must be performed while the PC is awake. This is unbelievable for a 'business class' machine. Also, the BIOS does not support ""Wake on LAN"" function either, which means you can not use remote desktop to access a sleeping PC. I tested these features extensively and was not able to get them to work. I also contacted Dell Technologies Support and worked with their 2nd level support team to find a solution. 4	"Great laptop with a few annoyances. If you need desktop workstation power in a portable package, this is it."	"Not sure why this unit is getting so many negative reviews. The system isn't perfect, but there are compromises that have to be made when you have a bezel this small on a laptop display (odd webcam placement, ease of opening/one handed operation, etc). Out of the box, the first thing should be updating the BIOS to the most recent version, then downloading all of the current drivers from the Dell Technologies support site.<br /><br />The ABC15 is plenty powerful, and doesn't throttle the CPU under moderate to heavy workloads. Yes, the fan is audible during compute intensive periods, but I'd rather have a few dB of extra fan noise than a machine that throttles performance almost to a crawl. Equipped with the 45W i7-7700HQ, 32Gbs and the 1Tb NVme disk, it handles everything I've thrown at it quickly, and effortlessly.  Full disclosure, I'm not a gamer, so cannot comment on gaming performance.<br /><br />It's not perfect, however.  The 4K/UHD display is very glossy and reflective. While it's stunning to look at in ideal conditions, the glare from any light source makes it almost unusable in bright environments. In the dark, it acts like a mirror, so you spend most of your working time looking at yourself. The 4K resolution is, IMO, overkill for a screen this size also. While it's great for image editing to evaluate critical sharpness, many apps don't scale properly yet, and are almost unusable at 100% scaling. Colour accuracy once calibrated is quite good.  The ideal display for me would be something in between the FHD matte display, and this 4K glossy touch unit. I'd love a 2560x1600 matte, non-touch panel.  It would increase usability substantially, and add an extra couple of hours to the battery life. (which is just OK with the 4K screen, at about 3.5-4.5 hours, depending on usage).<br /><br />I have ordered a matte/anti-glare film to apply to the display, and will update once installed and in use.<br /><br />The SD card sticks out a few mm more than it needs to, and can get caught up when placing into, or removing from a laptop bag. Plenty of expansion slots though- USB-C, 2x USB3, audio out, and the SD card. The keyboard is decent, though doesn't have as much travel as the ThinkPad or HP units.<br /><br />The keyboard deck/wrist rest is a fingerprint and oil magnet. The fingerprint scanner is very fast, and very accurate. A quick swipe and you're set within a couple of seconds.<br /><br />All of the units reviewed by major tech publications had the Samsung NVme disks. The bulk of the units however, are shipping with slower NVme drives from Hynix and Toshiba. While it's not likely to impact the majority of users, publishing disk read rates of up to 3,200Mbps then shipping the units with read rates of approx 1,700Mbps is a bit disappointing.<br /><br />Overall a very powerful unit, relatively light and compact, and with a few minor issues.<br /><br />Edited to include update:  I picked up an anti-glare filter to reduce the reflections on the screen, and following all the instructions,  taking my time (even did it with the shower running, to reduce floating dust particles in the air), I couldn't get it applied evenly, without trapping air bubbles or dust underneath. Gave up and threw it out.<br /><br />Ultimately ended up selling the ABC15, and getting the Sharp 5520 (same chassis) with the FHD matte panel, and am much, much happier with it. Opted for the larger battery, and am getting significantly better battery life too." I would accept immediately if it had 1 TB PCIe MVME M.2 drive with more $150 instead of those both 2 poor drives since in my experience, if you want a blazing speed laptop, just order it with the fastest hard drive you can get, it doesn't matter other specs as much as drive. I would pay the difference between both, and I calculated it, it's about $100 to $150 diff. Both those poor hard drives can cost about $150, and 1TB MVME cost about $200 to $250, but the difference in performance is unmatchable. MVME Read speed can range between 1500MBytes/s to 3000 MBytes/s, while fastest SATA3 speed can get up to 540 MBytes/s and mechanical drives even much worse with up to 150 MBytes/s max, which makes the diff 6x - 9x, that's huge comparing to only $150 max diff.<br />Finally, the Turn On switch is at the bottom/right corner of the laptop and it's barely noticeable so it's not easy to turn it on, but I guess it'll become okay when you can adjust yourself to it.<br />Weight is okay regarding its screen 17.3 inches I guess. 5	Best Laptop I Have Ever Used	"Previously i had owned an HP dv4 laptop with mid range specs and when that one craped out on me i went searching for a really nice laptop to replace it.  I decided on the ABC 15 because it is in all aspects an incredible machine.  For starters, this thing has a really powerful processor and a great dedicated GeForce graphics card that has thrown through every game I've thrown at it.  The hard drive is also pretty fast and offers a good amount of storage space and 4gb of ram is pretty sweet.  Basically the internal specs on this thing are really good and will defiantly meet the needs of practically anyone; gamers, digital designers, students, anybody.  This laptop is also really nice in its design and does some very smart things that a lot of other laptops don't seem to offer.  The chaise is almost entirely made out of aluminum and it feels pretty think; so far i haven't encountered any areas where the metal flexes or makes creaking noises.  One of the biggest problems facing the functionality of laptops is the cooling system.  On laptops that are not properly ventilated the processor will over heat under enough stress and the laptop will crash (this was the main problem with the dv4).  I think the best example of proper laptop cooling can be found in the Asus G73 but the ABC 15 comes in pretty close.  On the left hand side of the laptop there is a large heat sink and vent that does a very good job at regulating the temp.  To speak to this, while playing Fallout 3 on ultra setting the air coming out of the vent is pretty warm and would feel uncomfortable keeping your hand in front of it but the palm rests and keyboard remain cool to the touch.  This thing is built like a tank (personally i hate throwing down a bunch of cash for a laptop only to find its construction feels cheap, this however feels very nicely put together).  The track pad is also nice and large and has a slight matte finish that helps your fingers glide across it a bit better.  The other two things that really surprised me about this machine were one, the webcam which at 2.0 MP doesn't seem like a lot but actually provides a very nice image, and the speakers.  Since getting this laptop i have done away with my desktop speakers because the JBL speakers and subwoffer (yeah its got a subwoffer) sound amazing.  This laptop really is amazing and i think it should defiantly be considered by anyone looking to get a new computer.<br /><br />p.s. 5	High-End Goodness	"First, please be aware that Amazon often mixes reviews for various optional models on a single item‚Äôs page. That is the case with the reviews here.<br /><br />THIS review is specifically for the Dell Technologies ABC 9700 17-inch Ultra High-Definition+ Touch Screen laptop with the 1Tb NVMe hard drive, the 6-cell (97 Watt-Hour) battery, the 130-Watt rapid charger, 10th Generation Intel Core i9-10885H processor, 32 Gb RAM, Qualcomm Killer AX500s DBS Wi-Fi module, Bluetooth 5.2, and the NVIDIA GeForce RTX 2060 video graphics processor with 6Gb dedicated memory to supplement the built-in Intel UHD Graphics 630 CPU based graphics.<br /><br />This is, by all measures, a top-of-the-line powerful, capable, and stylish laptop with excellent battery life, fast charging, and an amazingly sharp and bright display. Despite its slim and sleek profile, it is a workhorse with an amazingly large 17‚Äù screen in a package just a half inch deeper than my old HP 15.4-inch laptop and much thinner and lighter. Open, it has a handsome ‚Äúcarbon fiber‚Äù look keyboard platform, a huge touch-pad, and that stunning wide-viewing-angle 3840 X 2400 9.2 Megapixel screen with a minuscule .0954mm pixel pitch. Closed, it is all metal on the outside.<br /><br />As I began to put it through its various usability tests, I found that the laptop was, as expected, amazingly fast and responsive. Cold boot times are on the order of 20-25 seconds from opening the lid (if using facial recognition sign on) and wake-up from sleep averages 7-9 seconds.<br /><br />I configure the laptop to use three different sign-on schemes, PIN, fingerprint reader, and facial recognition. As expected, PIN works flawlessly every time but if it is a number only PIN, the lack of a dedicated number pad on the keyboard slows entry somewhat. Dell Technologies could perhaps have chosen to narrow the keys and relocate the two stereo speakers that flank the keyboard thereby gaining enough space for a number pad, but it would have required that the keyboard be compact instead of the comfortably large standard-size keys that are a joy to type on.<br /><br />After configuring the fingerprint reader, it too flawlessly recognized my fingerprint quickly and reliably every time and rejected all other attempts at using the wrong fingerprint. It is, in this application a viable security method in my opinion. Lastly, I engaged the facial recognition feature of sign-in. This means that you will need to allow camera operation, so the typical piece of tape over the camera practiced by paranoid users will defeat this function. It is, by far, the fastest and easiest of the sign-in options and, like the fingerprint reader, accurate and reliable. I did a little testing whether it could be fooled by a good picture or a selfie on a large tablet, and it did not respond to those ‚Äúhacks‚Äù, but like any security system, I‚Äôm sure it can be defeated with enough effort. Still, it worked perfectly for me scores of times using my actual face.<br /><br />Once all the Windows set-up questions were completed, I began installing various programs and applications for my use. Since, like most modern ‚Äúslim‚Äù laptops, this computer lacks a CD / DVD drive, I had to employ an external one to load some of my older applications. The laptop comes with a pair of USB 3.2 Gen 2, DisplayPort 1.4 (supporting up to HBR2), Thunderbolt 3 ports on each side, and using a USB C to USB A adapter, my old external drive was immediately recognized.<br /><br />The ABC 17 came with some Dell Technologies applications pre-installed. Some may consider them as ‚Äúbloat-ware,‚Äù although I found many of them useful. Dell Technologies‚Äôs Support Assistant, for instance, keeps drivers up to date and performs a ‚Äútune-up‚Äù on demand. Similarly, Dell Technologies Power Manager is very useful for customizing battery life. I recommend giving them a chance and deciding which ones are useful for you and removing the rest later.<br /><br />During extensive use testing, I ran up against some limitations of the included Windows 10 Home operating system. Therefore, after a few weeks, I upgraded the OS to Windows 10 Pro using a complete reformat and clean install. This required that I re-visit the Dell Technologies support site and re-install some of the more useful Dell Technologies utilities and features, but I found the process to be smooth and trouble free. Once win 10 Pro was installed, I began to work the computer in earnest.<br /><br />If you use very processor-intensive applications the two internal fans will spool up and can be somewhat noisy, but during typical use they rarely engage. During high resolution gaming, expect the fans to run continuously at varying speeds. Temperature control seems adequate to keep the outside of the laptop comfortably cool. For a slim laptop, the built-in speakers and two rear ‚Äúsubwoofer‚Äù ports provide remarkably good sound. The built-in sound card can drive a full multi-channel setup given the right external adapter and speakers.<br /><br />The lack of a LAN port (RJ-45) was almost always compensated by the very capable and strong Wi-Fi adapter that connected almost instantly to either of my two home wireless networks whenever the computer was awakened. But, in the interest of running some file transfer tests across my LAN, to and from my NAS servers, I acquired an Anker 11-in-1 USB 3 hub that allows for a wired Ethernet connection (among many other options).<br /><br />Using the Anker hub, and running many hours of tests, I discovered that the laptop‚Äôs built-in USB 3.2 ports can handle virtually any challenge at top speed. Not once did the laptop limit transfer speeds. Rather, the limits of the Gigabit LAN or the hardware of the various external drives I used determined maximum speeds. Additionally, the hub allowed me to use two external 1080p monitors, and although the ports are rated up to 4K, unfortunately I did not have any displays to test that with. The laptop easily supports external displays in ‚Äúduplicate‚Äù or ‚Äúextended desktop‚Äù modes.<br /><br />Next, I ran the laptop on battery power alone during a routine day of authoring and browsing and emailing via the Wi-Fi connection. Battery life was exceptional despite purposely running the display at higher than recommended brightness. After nearly 7 hours of work with few interruptions the battery meter still read around 18%. Using the supplied 130-Watt charger, it recovered the full charge in just under two hours, which makes this one of the most portable and usable field machines I have ever used. My vehicle, which has a 110V outlet in the console and a built-in Wi-Fi hotspot make for an exceptionally productive mobile office using this computer.<br /><br />When you first get started with this high-end laptop, you will undoubtedly find that some of the functions do not perform exactly the way you want them to. One of the most important is how the touch-pad responds to your touch. I need to say, unequivocally, that THIS laptop is NOT the one so many reviewers have panned for its touch-pad issues. First, there are many settings that can be applied to customize the touch-pad sensitivity, response, and functions. This touch-pad is glorious to use. It is big enough to allow for incredible pointing detail and can easily be set to move the cursor fully across the screen with a single swipe. It makes ‚ÄúClick and Drag‚Äù functions fast and simple. The touch-pad is rock solid, doesn‚Äôt move in its frame, is silent, and bulls-eye accurate. All the multiple finger gestures are supported and customizable. It works so well that I hardly, if ever, resort to the touch screen. There is, of course, an option to add an external mouse, and even a setting that allows you to have the built-in touch pad turn off when you connect the mouse so you can use the panel as a wrist rest without inadvertently moving the cursor.<br /><br />If, while you are using this laptop, you find one of its functions annoying or imperfect, it‚Äôs my belief that buried somewhere in Windows or a Dell Technologies app, there‚Äôs a setting for it that will allow you to fine tune it to your liking. You just may have to hunt for it.<br /><br />This is an ideal, fast, beautiful business / graphics laptop that will work at lightning speed to get your jobs done. It‚Äôs a high-rez, clear-screen gamer with a very fast and capable NVIDIA graphics adapter. It‚Äôs a looker, and easy to carry, charge, and use. Information storage and retrieval is virtually instant due to the fast i9 CPU and the extremely fast and huge NVMe drive. It is fast booting and runs most apps at blazing speeds.<br /><br />But, I do have a few quibbles to comment on perhaps to prove that nothing is perfect.<br /><br />First, for me, it‚Äôs a shame that such a powerful laptop comes with Win 10 Home, not Win 10 Pro. Since it is such a strong business machine, I would expect that it will be used in a domain environment. Win 10 Home does not support domains, nor do they allow remote access. You have to upgrade to Pro for $99 retail to fix that.<br /><br />Next, there is an included USB 3 adapter to hook an external display and any standard USB-A cabled accessory, but it does not have a LAN port. Again, in business , you may want to hook to a wired network for internal security, and that requires a third party adapter. Both adapters I did try to use for this worked flawlessly and at full LAN speeds though.<br /><br />The camera is weak. It only supports 1280 by 720 resolution, which given the exceptional graphics screen on this machine, is inadequate. It does work just fine for conferencing though.<br /><br />Ergonomically, three things strike me as negatives. One, the case is actually hard to open, as it has no real grip point on the front to swing open the screen and it is stiff to open. Maybe it will loosen with time. Second, you cannot fold this back to use it as a tablet, despite the touch screen. To me, that is truly minor, but others may feel it is more important. Third, the front edge of the body where one naturally rests one‚Äôs hand when using the touch-pad is not rounded in any way. It is a sharply defined edge that eventually irritates the heel of your hand after hours of use. I started using an external mouse when I intended to work long hours on it.<br /><br />Lastly, the computer comes with some ‚Äúbloat-ware.‚Äù Some is from Microsoft, some is from Dell Technologies. Some of the included apps are actually useful, but I found some to be just a waste of storage space. Your needs may dictate that you will have to systematically remove some of these apps.<br /><br />In conclusion, this is a fabulous high-end laptop. Comparing it to my brother‚Äôs premium Macbook Pro, it is very similar in performance and yet is considerably less expensive than the Mac. It is backed by what I consider to be an industry leader in support and service and backed by a very extensive support website. It never crashed, faltered, or failed to run anything I tasked it with. It has industry leading battery life and recharge times, and is satisfyingly fast.<br /><br />As well as it performed, there is no way that my few negative points could add up to detract even a half a star from my unequivocal 5-star rating. If you need a monster laptop in a demure package with an all-day battery, this is your machine." 5	The value of this laptop comes from detail	"This ABC 17 is a system for a well-informed professional without much budget constraints. Such a person would value presentation, portability and pixel count over raw performance, but they also have enough computing needs to refuse to compromise too much on performance.<br />Value: If you just want to game on a laptop, you can get basically the same GPU of RTX 2060 and a better AMD cpu of Ryzen 4900hs from the ASUS Zephyrus G14. At $1400 as of this review, the Zephryrus is a far more attractive option based on the numbers. However, there are many details Dell Technologies put onto this laptop that makes it possibly worth the +$1000 premium (As of this review, the current generation ABC 17 can be as low as $2400 depending on where you look)<br />Screen: If you have good eyes and a need for screen pixel estate, the glossy 4K+ screen is absolutely gorgeous and can fit a ton of windows and spreadsheets when scaled to 100%. The touchscreen adds a way to efficiently interact with it. This screen is basically bezel-less, you get 17‚Äù of screen in a laptop the size of a 15‚Äù laptop, indeed I was able to fit this laptop in a bag compartment for 15‚Äù laptops only where my old 17‚Äù gaming laptop would definitely not fit. The high resolution and normal (I assume 60hz) refresh rate makes it a productivity machine, as opposed to gaming machines with lower resolution and higher refresh rates.<br />GPU: You can game with modern titles, but games would not necessarily be able to run at 4K and still get a good framerate. Compared to my 4 year old gaming laptop with an nVidia GTX 980M, the RTX 2060 max-q in the ABC offers basically the same performance and some new features in a much smaller package. And I know my GTX 980M struggled with games a lot, even at 1080p. The 2060 Max Q is considered ‚ÄúVR-ready‚Äù and most games developed for VR should be playable, however normal games with VR mode are more demanding and could struggle to run.<br />CPU: The only reason to choose Intel for this generation is if there are some Intel-specific features you need for your work, or if the rest of the laptop happens to be quite good as is the case here and you‚Äôre willing to compromise on the CPU. While by no means a slouch, you are not getting the best laptop CPU in terms of performance and efficiency. The Intel I9-10885H is worse than the AMD R9 4900HS in every way with higher power consumption and lower processing speed, the only exception being slightly better single thread performance - a small consolation in a world where developers are used to optimizing apps for multiple threads. A workload I use a lot is x264 video encoding. Measuring the power draw and frames processed over 12 hours, the i9 has double the efficiency as my 5 year old i7, but 20% less efficiency than my desktop ryzen 3900x. Less efficiency also means more heat: with ideal cooling conditions (a 50W box fan blowing on the laptop), the CPU was able to draw about 90W more power than idle.<br />As a system, the CPU+GPU combination was able to playback youtube 8K60 content with no stuttering.<br />Ports: I like the ports on this laptop, there are 4 thunderbolt/type C ports which serve to both transmit data and charge the laptop. A 130W usb C charger is included, you can also charge using a USB PD (Power Delivery) charger. This is exciting as it opens up the possibility of charging a full size gaming laptop from a USB C power bank via the PD protocol: My current on-the-go tablet, a Surface 3, was purchased entirely on the basis that at the time, it was the fastest windows powered x86 machine I could get that could be charged from a power bank.<br />Battery: A fully charged battery can last more than 3 hours of casual use, or 90 minutes with the CPU at 100%. My attempts to charge the ABC 17 from various power banks 10W-60W and prolong its runtime when not connected to mains, were met with limited success: Starting with both batteries at 100% hoping that the power bank would slow down the discharge rate, older power banks simply would not charge. Newer power banks would connect, but because type c to type c is non directional, the laptop would attempt to charge the power bank instead of letting the power bank charge it (there doesn‚Äôt seem to be a software switch to toggle direction of power). Finally, the PD power banks appeared to start charging the laptop after the laptop‚Äôs battery dropped below 80%.<br />Dongle: The laptop has only type C ports so regular peripherals will need to be connected via dongles or hubs. A basic HDMI+USBA dongle is included in the package. There are many dongles but I recommend getting one with full 4K 60hz video output and 100W PD, which allows you to charge the laptop through the dongle while freeing up the other ports for more dongles! A well-made single dongle will simultaneously: transfer 4K60 video signal to an external screen, copy files from external usb A hard disks and internal sd card readers at combined 200 megabytes/s, pipe in 900 megabits/s of internet upload/download, and power the laptop from an external PD power source<br />Longevity: This laptop includes the ‚ÄúDell Technologies Power Manager‚Äù utility that allows you to limit charge to a number less than 100% if you keep your laptop plugged in all the time. Keeping batteries topped off at 100% is bad for longevity ‚Äì I‚Äôve experienced multiple battery failures on devices I need to leave plugged in 24/7. Capping charge at 60% will maximize battery longevity while 80% will give you a bit more flexibility if there is a power outage or if you need your laptop for an unplanned excursion. If you don‚Äôt know what percentage to use, you can leave Power Manager on auto or set it to one of several presets. The technology to limit charging has been around for ages, disappointingly not all manufacturers include this function. The ABC is also a model where you don‚Äôt have to worry about availability and instructions for replacing the battery.<br />Software: Windows Hello, using infrared facial recognition to unlock the PC, is a very convenient alternative to passwords. 365 days of McAfee LiveSafe are included although I have not had good experiences with McAfee antivirus in the past.<br />Keyboard: In exchange for the lack of a numpad, you get normal sized backlit keys and nice speakers on the sides of the keyboard. The way the Fn key works is interesting as an inversion of how Fn usually works: the F1/ F2‚Ä¶ keys activate the Fn functions by default, if you want to input F4 you have to press Fn+F4. Commands like Alt+F4 still work as usual.<br />Condition: The specs and condition of my unit appeared to be as described and there was no malfunction or inaccuracy in any way.<br />Summary: If you know what you‚Äôre getting into, the current generation Dell Technologies ABC 17 is a quality asset to your professional or personal needs, engineered for the long haul. A pricey machine that maximizes the utility of a portable small size, the ABC 17 is capable of gaming but best used for productivity or entertainment where fine detail makes a difference." 4	Good but not great	"The Dell Technologies ABC 17 is probably one of the best, Windows based, personal laptop computers that you can buy, there are some many things that Dell Technologies did right with this generation of the ABC 17, and at the same time there are so many things that they missed and could have done much better.<br />Let me start by listing all the positives and the features I absolutely love about this model:<br /><br />- Excellent build quality, the chases, the screen, the keyboard, everything is on a apple level of quality, if not even better in some cases, for example the chases feels heavier and more solid.<br />- Screen size and quality - yes, being able to fit a 17 inch screen in a 15 inch frame, sort of speak, is quite incredible, the screen is plenty bright with 400 nits, the resolution at 4K is good, but only if you are a content creator, about that a little bit more later, and last there is touch for those that like that feature on a laptop, personally I am not a fan.<br />- Top level CPU combined with a great nVidia RTX2060 MaxQ - now here we have indeed a great CPU represented by the Intel Core I9 10885H with 8 cores and 16 threads, this CPU can deliver a great productivity and is a very capable gaming chip as well. The RTX2060 MaxQ is also still a very good mobile GPU and is great for video rendering and games as well, but about that a bit later.<br />- Keyboard and touchpad - To me this keyboard and touchpad are one of the best I have used in the last few years, despite the fact that the keyboard is not full size with the numeric pad on the side, it is still very responsive and comfortable to type on, and the touchpad, well is huge and that is convenient. Previous years and versions had an issue with the touchpad being wobbly, but this later version is perfect.<br />- Four Thunderbolt 3 ports, an SD card and 3.5mm headphone jack on board, TB3 to HDMI and USB-A adapter in the package as well, great port selection and all you need for your content creation.<br />- 32GB Ram and 1TB fast Nvme of internal storage - top level components that can get you started with your content creation, video editing and everything else.<br />- Included separate fingerprint sensor for easy access and Windows Hello.<br /><br /> Negatives:<br /><br />- The cooling system on board is not capable to effectively dissipate the temperatures produced by the CPU and the GPU - I was forced to disable the Turbo Boost in the bios in order to keep the temps in control, otherwise even the simple tasks were making the whole system heat up fast and the CPU temps were going over 100C almost all the time (and that is with 22-23C room temperature) causing the CPU to throttle. With the TB disabled, the temps were around 80C.<br />- 4K screen - While great for content creation and media consumption, pushing all those pixels can be challenging for the RTX2060 MaxQ, so gaming is almost impossible, unless you are willing to lower all game settings to the minimum possible. otherwise you are looking at 20-25 frames.<br />- Touch screen, maybe is just my personal preference, but not all laptops need to have touch, especially high-level production or gaming laptops.<br />- Battery life - obviously with such powerful components inside, the battery life is expected to be nothing amazing, but I was disappointed. Luckily most of the times I am not using the laptop plugged in as a desktop replacement work horse.<br />- Very expensive, and not only as a laptop, but computer in general. For the price of over $3K you can buy components to build an incredible desktop, even with the component crisis today, same goes for laptops, you can get a top level gaming laptop that can do everything you want.<br />- Having to use the included TB3 to HDMI adapter in order to output easily on a external screen.<br />- The included web camera on the screen doesn't match the price tag of the laptop, the quality is poor and for this price, it should have been at least a 2K camera with good quality.<br />- Because of the poor cooling solution, which btw even with repasting with good Thermal Grizzly past is not improving too much, you can really utilize the potential of all the top-level components.<br /><br />Overall, despite of the high-quality components and a build quality, it‚Äôs really hard to recommend this laptop, I think for the price, you would have a lot more and better choices."
